```c++
// a.h
#pragma once

// IWYU falsely suggests removing this header,
// which makes compilation fail.
#include "print.h"

struct A { void print(); };

template <>
void print(A) = delete;
```
```c++
// a.cpp
#include "a.h"

#include <iostream>

void A::print()
{
    std::cout << "A\n";
}
```
```c++
// print.h
#pragma once

#include <iostream>

template <typename T>
void print(T value) {
    std::cout << "Generic value: " << value << '\n';
}

template <>
inline void print(bool value) {
    std::cout << "Boolean value: " << (value ? "TRUE" : "FALSE") << '\n';
}
```

```
- #include "print.h"  // lines 5-5

---

(a.cpp has correct #includes/fwd-decls)
```

  1679	
  1680	  // If you say 'typedef Foo Bar', C++ says you just need to
  1681	  // forward-declare Foo.  But iwyu would rather you fully define Foo,
  1682	  // so all users of Bar don't have to.  We make two exceptions:
  1683	  // 1) The author of the typedef doesn't *want* to provide Foo, and
  1684	  //    is happy making all the callers do so.  The author indicates
  1685	  //    this by explicitly forward-declaring Foo and not #including
  1686	  //    foo.h.
  1687	  // 2) The typedef is a member of a templated class, and the
  1688	  //    underlying type is a template parameter:
  1689	  //       template<class T> struct C { typedef T value_type; };
  1690	  //    This is not a re-export because you need the type to
  1691	  //    access the typedef (via 'C<Someclass>::value_type'), so
  1692	  //    there's no need for the typedef-file to provide the type
  1693	  //    too.  TODO(csilvers): this is patently wrong; figure out
  1694	  //    something better.  We need something that doesn't require
  1695	  //    the full type info for creating a scoped_ptr<MyClass>.
  1696	  // As an extension of (2), if the typedef is a template type that
  1697	  // contains T as a template parameter, the typedef still re-exports
  1698	  // the template type (it's not (2)), but the template parameter
  1699	  // itself can be forward-declared, just as in (2).  That is:
  1700	  //   template<class T> struct C { typedef pair<T,T> value_type; };
  1701	  // iwyu will demand the full type of pair, but not of its template
  1702	  // arguments.  This is handled in VisitSubstTemplateTypeParmType.
  1703	  // Typedef underlying type is marked fwd-declarable by default, and the
  1704	  // aforementioned analysis is performed with 'IsProvidedTypeComponent'
  1705	  // function.
  1706	  bool VisitTypedefNameDecl(TypedefNameDecl* decl) {
  1707	    if (CanIgnoreCurrentASTNode())
  1708	      return true;
  1709	    current_ast_node()->set_in_forward_declare_context(true);
  1710	    return true;
  1711	  }
  1712	
  1713	  // Default type template arguments are forward-declarable, but can be provided
  1714	  // by the template author similarly to 'typedef' underlying types. They are
  1715	  // handled by 'IsProvidedTypeComponent'.
  1716	  bool VisitTemplateTypeParmDecl(TemplateTypeParmDecl*) {
  1717	    if (CanIgnoreCurrentASTNode())
  1718	      return true;
  1719	    current_ast_node()->set_in_forward_declare_context(true);
  1720	    return true;
  1721	  }
  1722	
  1723	  // If we're a declared (not defined) function, all our types --
  1724	  // return type and argument types -- are forward-declarable.  The
  1725	  // one exception required by the language is the throw types, which
  1726	  // we clean up in VisitType().
  1727	  // There are two more exceptions that iwyu imposes:
  1728	  // (1) iwyu asks the function author to provide the full type
  1729	  //     information for the return type.  That way the user doesn't
  1730	  //     have to.
  1731	  // (2) If any of our function parameters have a type with a
  1732	  //     non-explicit, one-arg constructor, or is a const reference to
  1733	  //     such a type, mark that type as not forward declarable.  The
  1734	  //     worry is that people might need the full type for the
  1735	  //     implicit conversion (the 'autocast'), for instance, passing
  1736	  //     in a char* to Fn(const StringPiece& foo) { ... }
  1737	  // Both of these iwyu requirements can be overridden by the function
  1738	  // author; for details, see CodeAuthorWantsJustAForwardDeclare.
  1739	  bool VisitFunctionDecl(FunctionDecl* decl) {
  1740	    if (CanIgnoreCurrentASTNode())
  1741	      return true;
  1742	
  1743	    if (decl->isThisDeclarationADefinition()) {
  1744	      // For non-member function definitions, report use of all previously seen
  1745	      // decls.
  1746	      if (decl->getKind() == Decl::Function) {
  1747	        const FunctionDecl* redecl = decl;
  1748	        while ((redecl = redecl->getPreviousDecl()))
  1749	          ReportDeclUse(CurrentLoc(), redecl, nullptr, UF_RedeclUse);
  1750	      }
  1751	    } else {
  1752	      // Make all our types forward-declarable.
  1753	      current_ast_node()->set_in_forward_declare_context(true);
  1754	    }
  1755	    return true;
  1756	  }
  1757	
  1758	  bool VisitVarDecl(VarDecl* decl) {
  1759	    if (CanIgnoreCurrentASTNode())
  1760	      return true;
  1761	
  1762	    if (decl->isThisDeclarationADefinition()) {
  1763	      // For variable definitions, report use of all previously seen decls with
  1764	      // external storage.
  1765	      const VarDecl* redecl = decl;
  1766	      while ((redecl = redecl->getPreviousDecl())) {
  1767	        if (!redecl->hasExternalStorage())
  1768	          continue;
  1769	        ReportDeclUse(CurrentLoc(), redecl, nullptr, UF_RedeclUse);
  1770	      }
  1771	    }
  1772	    return true;
  1773	  }
  1774	
  1775	  // Special handling for C++ methods to detect covariant return types.
  1776	  // These are defined as a derived class overriding a method with a different
  1777	  // return type from the base.
  1778	  bool VisitCXXMethodDecl(CXXMethodDecl* method_decl) {
  1779	    if (CanIgnoreCurrentASTNode())
  1780	      return true;
  1781	
  1782	    if (HasCovariantReturnType(method_decl)) {
  1783	      VERRS(6) << "Found covariant return type in "
  1784	               << method_decl->getQualifiedNameAsString()
  1785	               << ", needs complete type\n";
  1786	
  1787	      ReportTypeUse(CurrentLoc(), method_decl->getReturnType().getTypePtr(),
  1788	                    DerefKind::RemoveRefsAndPtr);
  1789	    }
  1790	
  1791	    return true;
  1792	  }
  1793	
  1794	  //------------------------------------------------------------
  1795	  // Visitors of types derived from Stmt.
  1796	
  1797	  // Catch statements always require the full type to be visible,
  1798	  // no matter if we're catching by value, reference or pointer.
  1799	  bool VisitCXXCatchStmt(CXXCatchStmt* stmt) {
  1800	    if (CanIgnoreCurrentASTNode())
  1801	      return true;
  1802	
  1803	    if (const VarDecl* exception_decl = stmt->getExceptionDecl()) {
  1804	      // Get the caught type from the decl via associated type source info to
  1805	      // get more precise location info for the type use.
  1806	      TypeLoc typeloc = exception_decl->getTypeSourceInfo()->getTypeLoc();
  1807	      const Type* caught_type = typeloc.getType().getTypePtr();
  1808	
  1809	      // Strip off pointers/references to get to the pointee type.
  1810	      ReportTypeUse(GetLocation(&typeloc), caught_type,

  5111	  // If you say 'typedef Foo Bar', then clients can use Bar however
  5112	  // they want without having to worry about #including anything
  5113	  // except you.  That puts you on the hook for all the #includes that
  5114	  // Bar might need, for *anything* one might want to do to a Bar.
  5115	  // TODO(csilvers): we can probably relax this rule in .cc files.
  5116	  // TODO(csilvers): this should really move into IwyuBaseASTVisitor
  5117	  // (that way we'll correctly identify need for hash<> in hash_set).
  5118	  // This is called from Traverse*() because Visit*()
  5119	  // can't call HandleFunctionCall().
  5120	  bool HandleAliasedClassMethods(TypedefNameDecl* decl) {
  5121	    if (CanIgnoreCurrentASTNode())
  5122	      return true;
  5123	
  5124	    const Type* underlying_type = decl->getUnderlyingType().getTypePtr();
  5125	    if (!AllTypesProvided(underlying_type, current_ast_node()->GetLocation()))
  5126	      return true;
  5127	    const Decl* underlying_decl = TypeToDeclAsWritten(underlying_type);
  5128	
  5129	    // We simulate a user calling all the methods in a class.
  5130	    if (const CXXRecordDecl* record_decl = DynCastFrom(underlying_decl)) {
  5131	      for (DeclContext::decl_iterator it = record_decl->decls_begin();
  5132	           it != record_decl->decls_end(); ++it) {
  5133	        FunctionDecl* fn_decl = nullptr;
  5134	        if (CXXMethodDecl* method_decl = DynCastFrom(*it)) {
  5135	          fn_decl = method_decl;
  5136	        } else if (FunctionTemplateDecl* tpl_decl = DynCastFrom(*it)) {
  5137	          fn_decl = tpl_decl->getTemplatedDecl();   // templated method decl
  5138	        } else {
  5139	          continue;    // not a method or static method
  5140	        }
  5141	        if (!this->getDerived().HandleFunctionCall(
  5142	                fn_decl, underlying_type, static_cast<Expr*>(nullptr)))
  5143	          return false;
  5144	      }
  5145	    }
  5146	    // We don't have to simulate a user instantiating the type, because
  5147	    // RecursiveASTVisitor.h will recurse on the typedef'ed type for us.
  5148	    return true;
  5149	  }

  5165	  bool VisitFunctionDecl(FunctionDecl* decl) {

  5179	            return Base::VisitFunctionDecl(decl);
  5180	          }
  5181	        }
  5182	      }
  5183	    }
  5184	    return Base::VisitFunctionDecl(decl);
  5185	  }

   601	
   602	  //------------------------------------------------------------
   603	  // (4) Add implicit text.
   604	  //
   605	  // This simulates a call to the destructor of every non-POD field and base
   606	  // class in all classes with destructors, to mark them as used by virtue of
   607	  // being class members.
   608	  bool TraverseCXXDestructorDecl(CXXDestructorDecl* decl) {
   609	    if (!Base::TraverseCXXDestructorDecl(decl))
   610	      return false;
   611	    if (CanIgnoreCurrentASTNode())
   612	      return true;
   613	    // We only care about calls that are actually defined.
   614	    if (!decl || !decl->isThisDeclarationADefinition())
   615	      return true;
   616	
   617	    // Collect all the fields (and bases) we destroy, and call the dtor.
   618	    set<const Type*> member_types;
   619	    const CXXRecordDecl* record = decl->getParent();
   620	    for (RecordDecl::field_iterator it = record->field_begin();
   621	         it != record->field_end(); ++it) {
   622	      member_types.insert(it->getType().getTypePtr());
   623	    }
   624	    for (CXXRecordDecl::base_class_const_iterator it = record->bases_begin();
   625	         it != record->bases_end(); ++it) {
   626	      member_types.insert(it->getType().getTypePtr());
   627	    }
   628	    for (const Type* type : member_types) {
   629	      // We only want those fields that are c++ classes.
   630	      if (const CXXRecordDecl* cxx_field_decl = type->getAsCXXRecordDecl()) {
   631	        if (const CXXDestructorDecl* field_dtor =
   632	                cxx_field_decl->getDestructor()) {
   633	          if (!this->getDerived().TraverseImplicitDestructorCall(
   634	                  const_cast<CXXDestructorDecl*>(field_dtor), type))
   635	            return false;
   636	        }
   637	      }
   638	    }
   639	    return true;
   640	  }
   641	
   642	  //------------------------------------------------------------
   643	  // (5) Add TraverseImplicitDestructorCall and HandleFunctionCall.
   644	
   645	  // TraverseImplicitDestructorCall: This is a callback this class
   646	  // introduces that is a first-class callback just like any AST-node
   647	  // callback.  It is used to cover two places where the compiler
   648	  // destroys objects, but there's no written indication of that in
   649	  // the text: (1) when a local variable or a temporary goes out of
   650	  // scope (NOTE: in this case, we attribute the destruction to the
   651	  // same line as the corresponding construction, not to where the
   652	  // scope ends).  (2) When a destructor destroys one of the fields of
   653	  // a class.  For instance: 'class Foo { MyClass b; }': In addition
   654	  // to executing its body, Foo::~Foo calls MyClass::~Myclass on b.
   655	  // Note we only call this if an actual destructor is being executed:
   656	  // we don't call it when an int goes out of scope!
   657	  //
   658	  // HandleFunctionCall: A convenience callback that 'bundles'
   659	  // the following Expr's, each of which causes one or more
   660	  // function calls when evaluated (though most of them are
   661	  // not a child of CallExpr):
   662	  //    * CallExpr (obviously)
   663	  //    * CXXMemberCallExpr
   664	  //    * CXXOperatorCallExpr -- a call to operatorXX()
   665	  //    * CXXConstructExpr -- calls a constructor to create an object,
   666	  //      and maybe a destructor when the object goes out of scope.
   667	  //    * CXXTemporaryObjectExpr -- subclass of CXXConstructExpr
   668	  //    * CXXNewExpr -- calls operator new and a constructor
   669	  //    * CXXDeleteExpr -- calls operator delete and a destructor
   670	  //    * DeclRefExpr -- if the declref is a function pointer, we
   671	  //      treat it as a function call, since it can act like one
   672	  //      in the future
   673	  //    * ImplicitDestructorCall -- calls a destructor
   674	  // Each of these calls HandleFunctionCall for the function calls
   675	  // it does.  A subclass interested only in function calls, and
   676	  // not exactly what expression caused them, can override
   677	  // HandleFunctionCall.  Note: subclasses should expect that
   678	  // the first argument to HandleFunctionCall may be nullptr (e.g. when
   679	  // constructing a built-in type), in which case the handler should
   680	  // immediately return.
   681	
   682	  // If the function being called is a member of a class, parent_type
   683	  // is the type of the method's owner (parent), as it is written in
   684	  // the source.  (We need the type-as-written so we can distinguish
   685	  // explicitly-written template args from default template args.)  We
   686	  // also pass in the CallExpr (or CXXConstructExpr, etc).  This may
   687	  // be nullptr if the function call is implicit.
   688	  bool HandleFunctionCall(FunctionDecl* callee, const Type* parent_type,
   689	                          const Expr* calling_expr) {
   690	    if (!callee)
   691	      return true;
   692	    if (ShouldPrintSymbolFromCurrentFile()) {
   693	      errs() << AnnotatedName("FunctionCall")
   694	             << PrintablePtr(callee) << PrintableDecl(callee) << "\n";
   695	    }
   696	    return true;
   697	  }
   698	
   699	  bool TraverseImplicitDestructorCall(CXXDestructorDecl* decl,
   700	                                      const Type* type_being_destroyed) {
   701	    if (CanIgnoreCurrentASTNode())
   702	      return true;
   703	    if (!decl)
   704	      return true;
   705	    if (ShouldPrintSymbolFromCurrentFile()) {
   706	      errs() << AnnotatedName("Destruction")
   707	             << PrintableType(type_being_destroyed) << "\n";
   708	    }
   709	    return this->getDerived().HandleFunctionCall(decl, type_being_destroyed,
   710	                                                 static_cast<Expr*>(nullptr));
   711	  }
   712	
   713	  bool TraverseCallExpr(CallExpr* expr) {
   714	    if (!Base::TraverseCallExpr(expr))
   715	      return false;
   716	    if (CanIgnoreCurrentASTNode())
   717	      return true;
   718	    FunctionDecl* func = expr->getDirectCallee();
   719	    if (!func)
   720	      return true;
   721	    // If the call makes use of default arguments, select exactly that
   722	    // redeclaration which specifies the first default argument used.
   723	    for (unsigned i = 0, ie = expr->getNumArgs(); i < ie; ++i) {
   724	      if (isa<CXXDefaultArgExpr>(expr->getArg(i))) {
   725	        func = GetRedeclSpecifyingDefArg(i, func);
   726	        break;
   727	      }
   728	    }
   729	    return this->getDerived().HandleFunctionCall(
   730	        func, TypeOfParentIfMethod(expr), expr);
   731	  }
   732	
   733	  bool TraverseCXXMemberCallExpr(CXXMemberCallExpr* expr) {
   734	    if (!Base::TraverseCXXMemberCallExpr(expr))
   735	      return false;
   736	    if (CanIgnoreCurrentASTNode())
   737	      return true;
   738	    return this->getDerived().HandleFunctionCall(expr->getDirectCallee(),
   739	                                                 TypeOfParentIfMethod(expr),
   740	                                                 expr);
   741	  }
   742	
   743	  bool TraverseCXXOperatorCallExpr(CXXOperatorCallExpr* expr) {
   744	    if (!Base::TraverseCXXOperatorCallExpr(expr))
   745	      return false;
   746	    if (CanIgnoreCurrentASTNode())
   747	      return true;
   748	
   749	    const Type* parent_type = TypeOfParentIfMethod(expr);
   750	    // If we're a non-member function -- bool operator==(MyClass a, MyClass b)
   751	    // -- we still want to have a parent_type, as if we were defined as
   752	    // MyClass::operator==.  So we go through the arguments and take the
   753	    // first one that's a class, and associate the function with that.
   754	    if (!parent_type) {
   755	      if (const Expr* first_argument = GetFirstClassArgument(expr))
   756	        parent_type = GetTypeOf(first_argument->IgnoreImpCasts());
   757	      // TODO(bolshakov): IgnoreParenImpCasts instead of IgnoreImpCasts?
   758	    }
   759	    return this->getDerived().HandleFunctionCall(expr->getDirectCallee(),
   760	                                                 parent_type, expr);
   761	  }
   762	
   763	  bool TraverseCXXConstructExpr(CXXConstructExpr* expr) {
   764	    if (!Base::TraverseCXXConstructExpr(expr))
   765	      return false;
   766	    if (CanIgnoreCurrentASTNode())
   767	      return true;
   768	
   769	    if (!this->getDerived().HandleFunctionCall(expr->getConstructor(),
   770	                                               GetTypeOf(expr),
   771	                                               expr))
   772	      return false;
   773	
   774	    // When creating a local variable or a temporary, but not a pointer, the
   775	    // constructor is also responsible for destruction (which happens
   776	    // implicitly when the variable goes out of scope).  Only when initializing
   777	    // a field of a class does the constructor not have to worry
   778	    // about destruction.  It turns out it's easier to check for that.
   779	    bool will_call_implicit_destructor_on_leaving_scope =
   780	        !IsCXXConstructExprInInitializer(current_ast_node()) &&
   781	        !IsCXXConstructExprInNewExpr(current_ast_node());
   782	    if (will_call_implicit_destructor_on_leaving_scope) {
   783	      if (const CXXDestructorDecl* dtor_decl = GetSiblingDestructorFor(expr)) {
   784	        if (!this->getDerived().TraverseImplicitDestructorCall(
   785	                const_cast<CXXDestructorDecl*>(dtor_decl), GetTypeOf(expr)))
   786	          return false;
   787	      }
   788	    }
   789	    return true;
   790	  }
   791	
   792	  bool TraverseCXXTemporaryObjectExpr(CXXTemporaryObjectExpr* expr) {
   793	    if (!Base::TraverseCXXTemporaryObjectExpr(expr))
   794	      return false;
   795	    if (CanIgnoreCurrentASTNode())
   796	      return true;
   797	
   798	    // In this case, we *know* we're responsible for destruction as well.
   799	    CXXConstructorDecl* ctor_decl = expr->getConstructor();
   800	    CXXDestructorDecl* dtor_decl =
   801	        const_cast<CXXDestructorDecl*>(GetSiblingDestructorFor(expr));
   802	    const Type* type = GetTypeOf(expr);
   803	    return (this->getDerived().HandleFunctionCall(ctor_decl, type, expr) &&
   804	            this->getDerived().HandleFunctionCall(dtor_decl, type, expr));
   805	  }
   806	
   807	  bool TraverseCXXNewExpr(CXXNewExpr* expr) {
   808	    if (!Base::TraverseCXXNewExpr(expr))
   809	      return false;
   810	    if (CanIgnoreCurrentASTNode())
   811	      return true;
   812	
   813	    const Type* parent_type = expr->getAllocatedType().getTypePtrOrNull();
   814	    // 'new' calls operator new in addition to the ctor of the new-ed type.
   815	    if (FunctionDecl* operator_new = expr->getOperatorNew()) {
   816	      // If the placement-new call makes use of default arguments, select
   817	      // exactly that redecl which specifies the first default argument used.
   818	      for (unsigned i = 0, ie = expr->getNumPlacementArgs(); i < ie; ++i) {
   819	        if (isa<CXXDefaultArgExpr>(expr->getPlacementArg(i))) {
   820	          // The 1st parameter is the size of the allocated type, there is not
   821	          // any corresponding argument.
   822	          CHECK_(i + 1 < operator_new->getNumParams());
   823	          operator_new = GetRedeclSpecifyingDefArg(i + 1, operator_new);
   824	          break;
   825	        }
   826	      }
   827	
   828	      // If operator new is a method, it must (by the semantics of
   829	      // per-class operator new) be a method on the class we're newing.
   830	      const Type* op_parent = nullptr;
   831	      if (isa<CXXMethodDecl>(operator_new))
   832	        op_parent = parent_type;
   833	      if (!this->getDerived().HandleFunctionCall(operator_new, op_parent, expr))
   834	        return false;
   835	    }
   836	    return true;
   837	  }
   838	
   839	  bool TraverseCXXDeleteExpr(CXXDeleteExpr* expr) {
   840	    if (!Base::TraverseCXXDeleteExpr(expr))
   841	      return false;
   842	
   843	    if (CanIgnoreCurrentASTNode())
   844	      return true;
   845	
   846	    const Type* parent_type = expr->getDestroyedType().getTypePtrOrNull();
   847	    // We call operator delete in addition to the dtor of the deleted type.
   848	    if (FunctionDecl* operator_delete = expr->getOperatorDelete()) {
   849	      // If operator delete is a method, it must (by the semantics of per-
   850	      // class operator delete) be a method on the class we're deleting.
   851	      const Type* op_parent = nullptr;
   852	      if (isa<CXXMethodDecl>(operator_delete))
   853	        op_parent = parent_type;
   854	      if (!this->getDerived().HandleFunctionCall(operator_delete, op_parent,
   855	                                                 expr))
   856	        return false;
   857	    }
   858	    const CXXDestructorDecl* dtor = GetDestructorForDeleteExpr(expr);
   859	    return this->getDerived().HandleFunctionCall(
   860	        const_cast<CXXDestructorDecl*>(dtor), parent_type, expr);
   861	  }
   862	
   863	  // This is to catch function pointers to templates.
   864	  // For instance, 'MyFunctionPtr p = &TplFn<MyClass*>;': we need to
   865	  // expand TplFn to see if it needs full type info for MyClass.
   866	  bool TraverseDeclRefExpr(DeclRefExpr* expr) {
   867	    if (!Base::TraverseDeclRefExpr(expr))
   868	      return false;
   869	    if (CanIgnoreCurrentASTNode())
   870	      return true;
   871	
   872	    if (FunctionDecl* fn_decl = DynCastFrom(expr->getDecl())) {
   873	      if (IsCallExprFunRef(current_ast_node_))
   874	        return true;
   875	      // If fn_decl has a class-name before it -- 'MyClass::method' --
   876	      // it's a method pointer.
   877	      const Type* parent_type = nullptr;
   878	      if (expr->getQualifier().getKind() == NestedNameSpecifier::Kind::Type)
   879	        parent_type = expr->getQualifier().getAsType();
   880	      if (!this->getDerived().TraverseFunctionIfInstantiatedTpl(
   881	              fn_decl, parent_type, expr))
   882	        return false;
   883	    }
   884	    return true;
   885	  }
   886	
   887	  /// Return whether this visitor should recurse into implicit
   888	  /// code, e.g., implicit constructors and destructors.
   889	  bool shouldVisitImplicitCode() const {
   890	    return true;
   891	  }

   893	 protected:
   894	  CompilerInstance* compiler() {
   895	    return compiler_;
   896	  }
   897	
   898	  // The currently active decl/stmt/type/etc -- that is, the node

  3029	    // If we're an overloaded operator, we can never do the iwyu check
  3030	    // before instantiation-time, because we don't know if we might
  3031	    // end up being the built-in form of the operator.  (Even if the
  3032	    // only operator==() we see is in foo.h, we don't need to #include
  3033	    // foo.h if the only call to operator== we see is on two integers.)
  3034	    if (!arbitrary_fn_decl || !arbitrary_fn_decl->isOverloadedOperator())
  3035	      ReportDeclUse(CurrentLoc(), first_decl);
  3036	    return true;
  3037	  }
  3038	
  3039	  // TODO(csilvers): handle some special cases when we're a
  3040	  // CXXDependentScopeMemberExpr (e.g. vector<T>::resize().).  If the
  3041	  // base class is a TemplateSpecializationType, get its TemplateDecl
  3042	  // and if all explicit specializations and patterns are defined in
  3043	  // the same file, treat it as an expr with only one decl.  May have
  3044	  // trouble with methods defined in a different file than they're
  3045	  // declared.
  3046	
  3047	  // If getOperatorNew() returns nullptr, it means the operator-new is
  3048	  // overloaded, and technically we can't know which operator-new is
  3049	  // being called until the template is instantiated.  But if it looks
  3050	  // like a placement-new, we handle it at template-writing time
  3051	  // anyway.
  3052	  bool VisitCXXNewExpr(CXXNewExpr* expr) {
  3053	    // Like in VisitUnresolvedLookupExpr(), we update processed_overload_locs
  3054	    // regardless of the value of CanIgnoreCurrentASTNode().
  3055	
  3056	    // We say it's placement-new if it has a single placement-arg, which _might_
  3057	    // be a pointer. In templates clang will just say it's a dependent type (or
  3058	    // dependent name, for function calls), so we use some heuristics to avoid
  3059	    // matching things like 'new (std::nothrow)' and 'new
  3060	    // (std::align_val_t(8))'. The pattern 'new (func())' can cause false
  3061	    // positives if the eventually looked up 'func()' does not return a pointer
  3062	    // type.
  3063	    const Expr* placement_expr = nullptr;
  3064	    if (!expr->getOperatorNew() && expr->getNumPlacementArgs() == 1) {
  3065	      placement_expr = expr->getPlacementArg(0);
  3066	    }
  3067	
  3068	    if (placement_expr &&
  3069	        (GetTypeOf(placement_expr)->isPointerType() ||
  3070	         GetTypeOf(placement_expr)->isArrayType() ||
  3071	         IsAddressOf(placement_expr) ||
  3072	         IsDependentNameCall(placement_expr))) {
  3073	      // Treat this like an UnresolvedLookupExpr.
  3074	      AddProcessedOverloadLoc(CurrentLoc());
  3075	      VERRS(7) << "Adding to processed_overload_locs (placement-new): "
  3076	               << PrintableCurrentLoc() << "\n";
  3077	      if (!CanIgnoreCurrentASTNode()) {
  3078	        // We have to 'make up' a full file path for 'new'.  We'll
  3079	        // parse it to '<new>' before using, so any path that does
  3080	        // that, and is clearly a c++ path, is fine; its exact
  3081	        // contents don't matter that much.
  3082	        OptionalFileEntryRef use_file = CurrentFileEntry();
  3083	        OptionalFileEntryRef file = compiler()->getPreprocessor().LookupFile(
  3084	            CurrentLoc(), "new", true, nullptr, RawFileEntry(use_file), nullptr,
  3085	            nullptr, nullptr, nullptr, nullptr, nullptr, false);
  3086	        if (file) {
  3087	          preprocessor_info().FileInfoFor(use_file)->ReportFullSymbolUse(
  3088	              CurrentLoc(), *file, "operator new");
  3089	        }
  3090	      }
  3091	    }
  3092	
  3093	    // We also need to do a varargs check, like for other function calls.
  3094	    if (CanIgnoreCurrentASTNode())
  3095	      return true;
  3096	    // ... only if this NewExpr involves a constructor call.
  3097	    const Expr* initializer = expr->getInitializer();
  3098	    if (const CXXConstructExpr* cce = DynCastFrom(initializer)) {
  3099	      ReportIfReferenceVararg(cce->getArgs(),
  3100	                              cce->getNumArgs(),
  3101	                              cce->getConstructor());
  3102	    }
  3103	    return true;
  3104	  }
  3105	
  3106	  bool VisitDeclRefExpr(DeclRefExpr* expr) {
  3107	    if (CanIgnoreCurrentASTNode())
  3108	      return true;
  3109	    // Report EnumName instead of EnumName::Item.
  3110	    // It supports for removing EnumName forward- (opaque-) declarations
  3111	    // from output.
  3112	    if (const auto* enum_constant_decl =
  3113	            dyn_cast<EnumConstantDecl>(expr->getDecl())) {
  3114	      const auto* enum_decl =
  3115	          cast<EnumDecl>(enum_constant_decl->getDeclContext());
  3116	
  3117	      // For unnamed enums, enumerator name is still preferred.
  3118	      if (enum_decl->getIdentifier())
  3119	        ReportDeclUse(CurrentLoc(), enum_decl);
  3120	      else
  3121	        ReportDeclUse(CurrentLoc(), enum_constant_decl);
  3122	    }
  3123	    return true;
  3124	  }
  3125

  3127	  // via ReportDeclUse() to make sure the definition of the function

  3129	  bool HandleFunctionCall(FunctionDecl* callee, const Type* parent_type,
  3130	                          const Expr* calling_expr) {

Here's the result of running `cat -n` on /testbed/iwyu.cc:
   330	// 4) Add appropriate implicit text.  iwyu acts as if all constructor
   331	//    initializers were explicitly written, all default constructors
   332	//    were explicitly written, etc, even if they're not.  We traverse
   333	//    the implicit stuff as if it were explicit.
   334	// 5) Add two callbacks that subclasses can override (just like any
   335	//    other AST callback): TraverseImplicitDestructorCall and
   336	//    HandleFunctionCall.  TraverseImplicitDestructorCall is a
   337	//    callback for a "pseudo-AST" node that covers destruction not
   338	//    specified in source, such as a destructor destroying one of the
   339	//    fields in its class.  HandleFunctionCall is a convenience
   340	//    callback that bundles callbacks from many different kinds of
   341	//    function-calling callbacks (CallExpr, CXXConstructExpr, etc)
   342	//    into one place.
   343	//
   344	// To maintain current_ast_node_ properly, this class also implements
   345	// VisitNestedNameSpecifier, VisitTemplateName, VisitTemplateArg, and
   346	// VisitTemplateArgLoc, which are parallel to the Visit*Decl()/etc
   347	// visitors.  Subclasses should override these Visit routines, and not
   348	// the Traverse routine directly.
   349	
   350	template <class Derived>
   351	class BaseAstVisitor : public RecursiveASTVisitor<Derived> {
   352	 public:
   353	  typedef RecursiveASTVisitor<Derived> Base;
   354	
   355	  // We need to create implicit ctor/dtor nodes, which requires
   356	  // non-const methods on CompilerInstance, so the var can't be const.
   357	  explicit BaseAstVisitor(CompilerInstance* compiler)
   358	      : current_ast_node_(nullptr), compiler_(compiler) {
   359	  }
   360	
   361	  virtual ~BaseAstVisitor() = default;
   362	
   363	  //------------------------------------------------------------
   364	  // Pure virtual methods that a subclass must implement.
   365	
   366	  // Returns true if we are not interested in the current ast node for
   367	  // any reason (for instance, it lives in a file we're not
   368	  // analyzing).
   369	  virtual bool CanIgnoreCurrentASTNode() const = 0;
   370	
   371	  // Returns true if we should print the information for the
   372	  // current AST node, given what file it's in.  For instance,
   373	  // except at very high verbosity levels, we don't print AST
   374	  // nodes from system header files.
   375	  virtual bool ShouldPrintSymbolFromCurrentFile() const = 0;
   376	
   377	  // A string to add to the information we print for each symbol.
   378	  // Each subclass can thus annotate if it's handling a node.
   379	  // The return value, if not empty, should start with a space!
   380	  virtual string GetSymbolAnnotation() const = 0;
   381	
   382	  //------------------------------------------------------------
   383	  // (1) Maintain current_ast_node_ and print each node.
   384	
   385	  // How subclasses can access current_ast_node_;
   386	  const ASTNode* current_ast_node() const {
   387	    return current_ast_node_;
   388	  }
   389	  ASTNode* current_ast_node() {
   390	    return current_ast_node_;
   391	  }
   392	  void set_current_ast_node(ASTNode* an) { current_ast_node_ = an; }
   393	
   394	  bool TraverseDecl(Decl* decl) {
   395	    if (!decl)
   396	      return true;
   397	    if (current_ast_node_ && current_ast_node_->StackContainsContent(decl))
   398	      return true;               // avoid recursion
   399	    ASTNode node(decl);
   400	    CurrentASTNodeUpdater canu(&current_ast_node_, &node);
   401	    if (ShouldPrintSymbolFromCurrentFile()) {
   402	      errs() << AnnotatedName(GetKindName(decl)) << PrintablePtr(decl)
   403	             << PrintableDecl(decl) << "\n";
   404	    }
   405	    return Base::TraverseDecl(decl);
   406	  }
   407	
   408	  bool TraverseStmt(Stmt* stmt) {
   409	    if (!stmt)
   410	      return true;
   411	    if (current_ast_node_ && current_ast_node_->StackContainsContent(stmt))
   412	      return true;               // avoid recursion
   413	    ASTNode node(stmt);
   414	    CurrentASTNodeUpdater canu(&current_ast_node_, &node);
   415	    if (ShouldPrintSymbolFromCurrentFile()) {
   416	      errs() << AnnotatedName(GetKindName(stmt)) << PrintablePtr(stmt)
   417	             << PrintableStmt(stmt) << "\n";
   418	    }
   419	    return Base::TraverseStmt(stmt);
   420	  }
   421	
   422	  bool TraverseType(QualType qualtype, bool traverse_qualifier = true) {
   423	    if (qualtype.isNull())
   424	      return true;
   425	    const Type* type = qualtype.getTypePtr();
   426	    if (current_ast_node_ && current_ast_node_->StackContainsContent(type))
   427	      return true;               // avoid recursion
   428	    ASTNode node(type);
   429	    CurrentASTNodeUpdater canu(&current_ast_node_, &node);
   430	    if (ShouldPrintSymbolFromCurrentFile()) {

  1561	                             const NamedDecl* used_decl,
  1562	                             const char* comment = nullptr,

  1565	    const NamedDecl* target_decl = used_decl;

  1570	      target_decl = shadow_decl->getTargetDecl();

  1585	    if (!report_using_decl_only) {

  1587	          used_loc, target_decl, use_flags, comment);
  1588	    }

  1590	    // Sometimes using a decl drags in a few other uses as well:
  1591

  1499	bool IsDefTplArgSpecified(const NamedDecl* tpl_param) {

  1502	           !type_param->defaultArgumentWasInherited();
  1503	  }

  1511	  CHECK_UNREACHABLE_("Not a template parameter");

  5469	    // TemplateSpecializationType when it's either the default argument of a
  5470	    // template template arg:
  5471	    //    template<template<class T> class A = TplNameWithoutTST> class Foo ...
  5472	    // or a deduced template specialization:
  5473	    //    std::pair x(10, 20); // type of x is really std::pair<int, int>
  5474	    // So that's the only cases we need to handle here.
  5475	    // TODO(csilvers): check if this is really forward-declarable or
  5476	    // not.  You *could* do something like: 'template<template<class
  5477	    // T> class A = Foo> class C { A<int>* x; };' and never
  5478	    // dereference x, but that's pretty unlikely.  So for now, we just
  5479	    // assume these default template template args always need full
  5480	    // type info.
  5481	    const ASTNode* ast_node = current_ast_node();
  5482	    if (ast_node->ParentIsA<DeducedTemplateSpecializationType>() ||

  5487	      // report the use if we can find a decl.

  5493	      }
  5494	    }
